text:
This is the BEST salad ever but after making it a few times I will say that you can do all these variations and it will be terrific but do NOT put the dressing into the fridge, leave it on the counter!  It will not be good, it will get creamy and stay on the salad like PASTE.  You can get the spinach (baby spinach is the best) and slice the strawberries with an egg slicer and toss ahead, in the fridge...but let the dressing sit on the counter, trust me.  Then toss immediately before eating.

text:
We loved this salad. I made it twice this weekend.  I added candied sliced almonds...  just add almond slices to a frying pan and lightly sugar the almonds,  add a few drops of water to this slowly and let it cook for a few minutes..  caramelizes to a crisp, sweet.  Very hot, be careful.  I also added the blue cheese, mentioned by other readers.   also..instead of using all that sugar, I substituted some honey for the sugar instead, which helped the dressing stick to the salad

Excellent Salad that brought rave reviews. Per others suggestions, I decreased the sugar by half. I only had red wine vinegar, so I used that. Dressing was tasty with just the right amount of sweetness for the salad. I served the dressing on the side. I added mandarin oranges, red onion and pecans!!!! Great salad!!!! Thanks Jerry.
Update: I tried the dressing with the raspberry balsamic vinegar and it was wonderful. I did increase the vinegar to a half cup and reduced the sugar in half. I think it could have used more sugar, but it was still a wonderful dressing and salad. I continue to add mandarin oranges, pecans and red onions. Great Salad!!!

text:
I hate to be the critic...  But I'm going to be completely honest.  The taste was a 4 star, but I could only eat a few bites of this salad.  I followed the recipe exactly.

First, it wasn't until I got into the recipe that I realized that this recipe took everything that was healthy about raw spinach and strawberries and turned it into a complete heart attack equating to McDonald's food on a bad day.

Literally, you are putting 1 full cup of super high fat oil mixed with sugar all over some healthy raw spinach and good healthy sweet fruit.  

Normally when I eat spinach salad, which is daily, I can eat a full plate of raw spinach with about 2 teaspoons of Italian dressing.  The whole thing is under 200 calories.  This recipe is immensely high fat and high sugar.

 Anyhow, I could only eat about 4 bites until I felt like "ugg".  I'm laying back now with my sugar rush feeling bad.  If I eat plain raw spinach with Italian, I feel like a million bucks.

I would highly consider re-doing this recipe.  The strawberries are a very nice touch, but all the sugar is a nightmare.

This is my opinion, and I do feel that we as a society eat way too much sugar.  This recipe is an example of how something very healthy is turned into a completely unhealthy meal.

I'm sorry, but I did think the flavor itself is 4 to 5 stars, but then again, oil + sugar taste good with anything.  Just like fried anything tastes good.

I have made this for years and it is always a huge hit.  For the dressing I use 1/4 cup oil, 2 T. sugar, 2 T. vinegar, 1/2 t. salt, and ground red pepper to taste.  I often add mandarin oranges and fresh blueberries.  Sugared almonds are a great addition as well.  Great with grilled steaks and chicken.  Thanks for all the great ideas for other variations!

text:
Great recipe, and it's the first I've save to my recipe box ;).  Here are my adjustments:

1. I used red wine vinegar instead of white vinegar

2. I used half the amount of sugar based on others recommendations

3. I added candied almonds... who doesn't love a little nut added to the mix?  I followed the recipe suggestion from another comment.

4. I added red pepper flakes... I like it spicy

5. I halfed the salad dressing recipe and added balsamic vinegar to the other half so that I could experience both... I preferred the one with balsamic vinegar

6.  This recipe is nothing without the poppy seeds ;). I had this sort of recipe at my wedding with a creamy poppy seed dressing and it was a hit!

And just to add... for all of the people that comment and say they hate when people adjust the recipe, I'm one of those that lives in the comments.  I'd prefer to see how people adjust, change and make the recipe their own.  It's what makes this site and the recipe soooo much better!

Enjoy.

This recipe is amazing!! I didn't use the seeds, but instead used crushed pecans. I used the full amount of sugar for the dressing (though many reviewers said not to) and thought it was perfect, but I do have a major sweet tooth! ;) I also used balsamic raspberry vinegar instead of the white wine vinegar.
I tossed together organic baby spinach, the sliced strawberries and pecans. I put the dressing into a bottle so we could pour it on our salads right before eating. I think that works better than mixing it all together, that way if there is some leftover it will last awhile in the fridge. I think next time I will try EVOO in place of the vegetable oil to make it a bit healthier!

text:
This is delicious and simple. I hate when people rate the recipe based on a ton of modifications; however, I did decrease the sugar to 1/4 cup, which seemed just right to me. I can't imagine it with the full amount in the recipe. 

When I made it a second time, I further decreased the oil by half (calorie-counting) and used olive oil (a "healthy" oil on my Weight Watchers). I also used balsamic vinegar rather than white due to personal preference.

In conclusion, I think the recipe is wonderful as it is (with half the sugar), but it's easy to make modifications and still come up with something terrific.

I made this salad for the first time tonight and took it to a BBQ where I did not know half the people. This salad was a huge hit. I had several people ask me for the recipe and the host informed me that many others were asking her for the recipe as well. I followed many others tips. I used two bags of bagged spinach leaves that I tore into smaller peices,a 2 pound container of strawberries, a handful of both feta and blue cheese chunks, 1 bag of real bacon pieces (in the salad topping isle),1 bag glazed walnuts (I chopped them up), 1/2 a red onion chopped, and I used balsamic vinegerette(sp?) in place of the white vineger. I had to use double the dressing and I poured it over the top and tossed it a good hour before the BBQ. Great Salad!

I liked this salad; the dressing was a little sweet for my taste and it got very thick after I refrigerated it. I ended up adding a little bit of Newmann's Own Balsamic Dressing to it, and the combo was terrific. I also added some chopped red onion and feta cheese - they went great with the other flavors and kicked the salad up a notch. It would also be nice with almonds or toasted pecans added. You can really suit this recipe to your own tastes - keep it simple or jazz it up. We'll make it again.

text:
My family practically licked the bowl clean!  Made this for Easter dinner, and even those who usually refuse to touch spinach with a 10 foot pole gobbled it up!  I even brought some to work for breakfast the next day and made my co-workers jealous!  It looks so fancy, yet is super simple and can be put together in the time it takes you to slice the strawberries.

Couple of things I changed - lowered the sugar by half (with the strawberries, it needs a more tart dressing, not so sweet).  Then sprinkled candied almonds (adds much needed crunchy texture) and crumbled feta cheese on top!  Also, tried balsamic vinegar in lieu of white wine vinegar - gave a totally different flavor to it.  

In the end, this salad is addictive!  So good, so healthy, and so easy.....  no reason you can't make it once a month... once a week?.... is once a day going too far??  :)

text:
This was absolutely delicious, light, and so healthy.  The colors were so vibrant and made for a beautiful salad.  I halved the recipe.  Thanks for all the helpful reviews.  I did add a couple of strawberries to the dressing and whipped it all up in the food processor.  I added slices of red onion, and toasted walnuts, and toasted the sesame seeds.  I kept the spinach seperate and made each salad.  There was no wilting of the spinach at all this way.  Per the reviews stating that the dressing was too sweet, since I halved the recipe, I used 1/4 cup EVOO, and 2 tbsp. of balsamic vinegar.  I like balsamic for its mild acidity and sweetness.  I added the sweetener last and added enough just to my personal taste.  I used sweetener in lieu of sugar and couldn't tell the difference.  This is so refreshing and the colors are wonderful!  I suggest adding the sugar at the end to taste.

My husband is in the strawberry business, so I'm always looking for recipes that include
strawberries.  This salad is wonderful!  We invited another couple over for dinner and I thought
I'd try out this recipe.  I added sliced red onion, toasted pecans, and gorgonzola cheese.  I also used balsamic
vinegar for part of the white wine vinegar.  I didn't have poppy seeds so I left that out.  The couple we invited over
for dinner are gourmet cooks, and they said this was the BEST salad they've ever tasted.  I will definitely be making
this salad on a regular basis!

city:

region:
None
country:
None
text:
I just made this for my granddaughter's 5th birthday at a park.  I made the dressing with 1/4 cup honey, 1/2 cup olive oil and 1/4 cup raspberrry balsalmic vinegar, toasted sesame seeds, 1/4 tsp paprika and a little bit of vanilla.  The salad I used 2 bags baby spinach, 1 bag spring mix with spinach,  2 containers strawberries, 1 container blueberries, 1/2 red onion sliced thin and 1 package of honey goat cheese that I froze for 15 minutes that made it easier to cut into small pieces.  I also did the sliced almonds toasted in a hot pan with sugar and a little water.  It was really delicious and special, the dressing is amazing with paprika! It does something unique to bring it all together.   I read many of the comments and kind of used what I thought sounded good so thank you to those that posted feedback for your help in making it perfect for me!  :)  I layered it, bag of spinach, sprinkle of berries, cheese and almonds, repeat with spring mix, then one more layer of spinach, berries, goat cheese, almonds on top.  Served the dressing on the side with a little mason jar so the salad wouldn't get soggy.  Next time I will add the poppy seeds, just forgot them at the store this time.  Will make again and again, and share this one for sure!

1/3 cup sugar is the magic amount! Made this yesterday for a potluck and reduced the sugar to 1/3 cup as some reviews said it was too sweet at 1/2 cup yet others said 1/4 cup wasn't enough. It was perfect! Used baby spinach, canola oil, balsamic vinegar and only sesame seeds as I didn't have poppy.  Added a large can of mandarin oranges and a kiwi as I didn't have quite enough strawberries. Well, I had NOTHING left to bring home with me yet others were leaving the potluck with gobs of left over food. I received many compliments and numerous persons asked for the recipe.  I'm making it again today for my family. This is an excellent, easy and healthy recipe that I will be using a lot. Thanks so much for sharing!

text:
I figured it out!  Wash and cut and slice strawberries first. Then mix up the dressing and set aside. I used honey instead of sugar. Wash the spinach gently and shake off excess water.  Spin any additional water off in a salad spinner. Then carefully mix the strawberries and spinach together in the salad spinner. Add just the amount of dressing you think that you will need to moisten the salad.  Then spin the strawberries and spinach again in the salad spinner to shake off any unneeded dressing.  Add poppy seeds, sesasme seeds and almonds and toss.  The salad will NOT be soggy and because you likely will not use all of the dressing, it will not be overly sweet!

text:
This salad is amazing! I used 1/4 cup agave in place of the white sugar and a mix of 1/4 c extra virgin olive oil and 1/4 c canola oil in place of the vegetable oil. I didn't have any white wine vinegar, so I used apple cider vinegar instead as I had it on hand. Also I had a bag of slivered almonds in the pantry, so I toasted some and topped the salad with them.  I noticed one reader mentioned that when she put the dressing in the fridge it hardened to a paste - I have experienced that myself when I have used only extra virgin olive oil in dressings ( it is so annoying!) but didn't have any issues with the lend of half canola half evoo, stayed nice and liquidy after being in the fridge overnight.

text:
Take it from someone who typically dislikes salad...this is a great recipe. I only gave it 4 stars because I made some changes to the recipe. I didn't have sesame or poppy seeds, so I made some candied pecans and almonds (throw them in a pan with sugar and a little water). I also did not have white wine vinegar, so I mixed half apple cider vinegar (all I had) with some red wine. I also replaced the 1/2 cup sugar with about 3 T honey. I didn't think the sugar would mix very well. The result was very delicious! I wasn't too sure about my vinegar/wine concoction, but it turned out great! Definitely will make again.

text:
I didn't give it a 5 star rating as I'm not sure how this would taste as it is. I had a very similar recipe but it included feta cheese - wouldn't be to everyone's liking but I think a creamy feta cheese goes wonderful with this. 

I have a mortar & pestle I use for Asian cooking. Crushing the poppy seeds so their flavour can meld in the dressing is better. Many people have no idea poppy seeds have a wonderful flavour & just use them as decoration. Crushing them will release their flavour into the dressing. Other than a few changes, the recipe for this salad would get 5 stars.

text:
I accidentally made a really yummy salad using this recipe as the base. I started off making a salad with romaine lettuce. I had too much spinach for the supper dish I was making, so I mixed some of it with the romaine. I added cucumber and sliced vidalia onion, and that's when it occurred to me that I should have made a spinach & strawberry salad, seeing as I have a basket of berries in the fridge. Well, I decided what the heck -- I added sliced strawberries to what I already had on the plates and made the dressing from this recipe (minus the seeds because I didn't have any, and with half the olive oil). I also added some cashews and crumbled goat cheese to the salad. And the final result was DELICIOUS!!!!!

The dressing really makes the salad -- but the flavours and textures of the other ingredients I added to the salad really worked well together.

I had an abundance of strawberries from the garden this year and was looking for things to do with them.  I was hesitant to make it because my husband and son are not salad people at all. text:
EVERYONE IS RIGHT! This is a fabulous salad! My husband, who doesn't care for spinach, says this could be a "restaurant" salad, and my daughter who hates every one of the ingredients except strawberries and sugar, said it was quite good, but she didn't LOVE it. I toasted the sesame seeds first and they got away from me a bit so some of them had a kind of burned flavor. The only sesame seeds I could find in the store were raw and the recipe doesn't specify toasted or not. I used Splenda instead of sugar and if I do that again I will use a little less. It took a bit of a search to find white wine vinegar, but it was worth it. I didn't want to mess with tearing the spinach so bought baby spinach which worked well but I was unsure about the amount to use. I served this salad to a group of 10 people and was delighted when the one with the most gourmet taste liked it the most.

I have used this recipe on a number of occassions.  Every time it gets complete RAVE reviews...even from the kids!  I substitute toasted chopped pecans for the sesame and poppy seads.  Yum!  I have also tried it substituting the strawberries for raspberries (yum) and when everything is out of season...even canned, drained mandarine wedges.  Wonderful!  The only thing to be careful of is to make sure you don't combine the dressing with the spinach until the absolute last minute.  It doesn't take long for the dressing to break down the spinach.

One of our favorite salads.  Ever.  It really doesn't need any more reviews, but I would like to add how much we love it.  For those who posted the most *helpful* critical reviews, if the addition of that much sugar is troublesome, cut it by half and it is still great.  I am always amazed by people who say they eat 2 tsp of dressing to a large salad, make the dressing as written and then say it's unhealthy.  Or even better, never make it and criticize it as being unhealthy.    Use your own common sense and reduce sugar/fat/whatever to what you already know you know are your own tastes.  Good gracious.  It's pretty simple.

text:
This is my favorite salad to bring for a summer picnic.  So why the two star rating?  Because I am rating it as it is written.  As written, there is was too much dressing, way too much sugar and not enough crunch.  To make it a 5 star, half the dressing and only use 1/4 of the sugar amount.  Okay, maybe you could use half the sugar if you like it sweet.  In order to give it crunch I added some sliced almonds..  I believe that we should rate a recipe as it is written.  If you have to alter amounts, add ingredients, etc, then you are making a different recipe.  As written...2 stars.

text:
DO NOT USE THIS MUCH DRESSING. This salad is great, simple and easy to make. Easy to add things you like ex. almonds. BUT, absolutely do not use this much dressing or you'll be drowning your salad in oil. It's not yummy. The dressing itself is actually really good - but you don't need to put it all on at once. I put about 1/4 of the dressing on and it was great that way. You can always leave more on the side if people wanted to put on more, but no one will!
